        }

          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;

        }

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        Description #

1

 

by adam...@gmail.com

 (

Jun 15, 2020

)
      

<option value="0" selected="">
        Description #1 by adam...@gmail.com (Jun 15, 2020)
      </option>


    




        

<select aria-label="Description history menu" hidden="">
          <!---->

        Description #1 by adam...@gmail.com (Jun 15, 2020)
      </option>
    <!---->
        </select>


      

<div class="select-container">
        <select aria-label="Description history menu" hidden="">
          <!---->
      <option value="0" selected="">
        Description #1 by adam...@gmail.com (Jun 15, 2020)
      </option>
    <!---->
        </select>
      </div>


      









We're writing to disclose vulnerabilities in the design and implementation of Linux's Spectre v1 (conditional branch) mitigations.  We're researchers from Tel Aviv University, Israel and are going to submit an academic paper on these issues for review.  If accepted, the paper will become publicly available in August, 2021.



<span class="line"><!---->We're writing to disclose vulnerabilities in the design and implementation of Linux's Spectre v1 (conditional branch) mitigations.  We're researchers from Tel Aviv University, Israel and are going to submit an academic paper on these issues for review.  If accepted, the paper will become publicly available in August, 2021.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We're reporting these issues here due to the the following statement on the Chrome VRP: "We'd also love to learn about bugs in third-party components that we ship or use (e.g. PDFium, Adobe Flash, Linux kernel)."



<span class="line"><!---->We're reporting these issues here due to the the following statement on the Chrome VRP: "We'd also love to learn about bugs in third-party components that we ship or use (e.g. PDFium, Adobe Flash, Linux kernel)."<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We have NOT checked if these Linux kernel issues are exploitable through Chrome,



<span class="line"><!---->We have NOT checked if these Linux kernel issues are exploitable through Chrome,<!----></span>



<br>





but believe they would be of interest to Google.  We're also reporting to 



<span class="line"><!---->but believe they would be of interest to Google.  We're also reporting to <!----></span>





security@kernel.org



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="mailto:security@kernel.org"><!---->security@kernel.org<!----></a>





 and to the Android team.  If this report is out of scope for



<span class="line"><!----> and to the Android team.  If this report is out of scope for<!----></span>



<br>





Chrome, please let us know who the relevant parties are within Google, if any.



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome, please let us know who the relevant parties are within Google, if any.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





---------------------



<span class="line"><!---->---------------------<!----></span>



<br>





All of the issues we're reporting are related to the fact that Spectre v1 attacks are not limited to bounds checking bypasses.  Misspeculation can lead the kernel to other invalid states that may result in memory disclosure. We specifically consider "speculative type confusion", where misspeculated code runs with some registers not containing their intended types.



<span class="line"><!---->All of the issues we're reporting are related to the fact that Spectre v1 attacks are not limited to bounds checking bypasses.  Misspeculation can lead the kernel to other invalid states that may result in memory disclosure. We specifically consider "speculative type confusion", where misspeculated code runs with some registers not containing their intended types.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Since there are several issues, we're breaking the report into 3 parts:



<span class="line"><!---->Since there are several issues, we're breaking the report into 3 parts:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  1. eBPF verifier vulnerability.



<span class="line"><!---->  1. eBPF verifier vulnerability.<!----></span>



<br>





  2. Compiler-introduced vulnerabilities.



<span class="line"><!---->  2. Compiler-introduced vulnerabilities.<!----></span>



<br>





  3. Indirect call-related vulnerabilities.



<span class="line"><!---->  3. Indirect call-related vulnerabilities.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is part 1 out of 3.



<span class="line"><!---->This is part 1 out of 3.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





-------



<span class="line"><!---->-------<!----></span>



<br>





Chrome Version: didn't check



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: didn't check<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: Linux - all



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Linux - all<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





-----------------



<span class="line"><!---->-----------------<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





eBPF verifier vulnerability:



<span class="line"><!---->eBPF verifier vulnerability:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The verifier only enumerates valid control-flow paths, and so it can miss type confusion caused by branch mispredictions.  Consider the following program:



<span class="line"><!---->The verifier only enumerates valid control-flow paths, and so it can miss type confusion caused by branch mispredictions.  Consider the following program:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





	// r0 = pointer to a map array entry



<span class="line"><!---->	// r0 = pointer to a map array entry<!----></span>



<br>





	// r6 = pointer to readable stack slot



<span class="line"><!---->	// r6 = pointer to readable stack slot<!----></span>



<br>





	// r9 = scalar controlled by attacker



<span class="line"><!---->	// r9 = scalar controlled by attacker<!----></span>



<br>





	1:  r0 = *(u64 *)(r0)	// cache miss



<span class="line"><!---->	1:  r0 = *(u64 *)(r0)	// cache miss<!----></span>



<br>





	2:  if r0 != 0x0 goto line 4



<span class="line"><!---->	2:  if r0 != 0x0 goto line 4<!----></span>



<br>





	3:  r6 = r9



<span class="line"><!---->	3:  r6 = r9<!----></span>



<br>





	4:  if r0 != 0x1 goto line 6



<span class="line"><!---->	4:  if r0 != 0x1 goto line 6<!----></span>



<br>





	5:  r9 = *(u8 *)(r6)



<span class="line"><!---->	5:  r9 = *(u8 *)(r6)<!----></span>



<br>





	6:  // leak r9



<span class="line"><!---->	6:  // leak r9<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Since line 3 runs iff r0 == 0 and line 5 runs iff r0 == 1, the verifier concludes that the pointer dereference on line 5 is safe.  But if the attacker trains both the branches to mispredict, such that the following is speculatively executed:



<span class="line"><!---->Since line 3 runs iff r0 == 0 and line 5 runs iff r0 == 1, the verifier concludes that the pointer dereference on line 5 is safe.  But if the attacker trains both the branches to mispredict, such that the following is speculatively executed:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





	r6 = r9



<span class="line"><!---->	r6 = r9<!----></span>



<br>





	r9 = *(u8 *)(r6)



<span class="line"><!---->	r9 = *(u8 *)(r6)<!----></span>



<br>





	// leak r9



<span class="line"><!---->	// leak r9<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





then the program will dereference an attacker-controlled value and leak its content.



<span class="line"><!---->then the program will dereference an attacker-controlled value and leak its content.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It's a little tricky to mistrain the branch predictor to predict this way, because the branches are mutually exclusive.  However, it can be done by training branches at congruent addresses in userspace which are not mutually exclusive.  That is, by training branches in userspace:



<span class="line"><!---->It's a little tricky to mistrain the branch predictor to predict this way, because the branches are mutually exclusive.  However, it can be done by training branches at congruent addresses in userspace which are not mutually exclusive.  That is, by training branches in userspace:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





	A:  if r0 != 0x0 goto line C



<span class="line"><!---->	A:  if r0 != 0x0 goto line C<!----></span>



<br>





	B:  ...



<span class="line"><!---->	B:  ...<!----></span>



<br>





	C:  if r0 != 0x0 goto line D



<span class="line"><!---->	C:  if r0 != 0x0 goto line D<!----></span>



<br>





	D:  ...



<span class="line"><!---->	D:  ...<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





such that addresses A and C map to the same branch prediction entries as those of the eBPF program's lines 2 and 4, respectively.



<span class="line"><!---->such that addresses A and C map to the same branch prediction entries as those of the eBPF program's lines 2 and 4, respectively.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Using these techniques, we built a proof-of-concept exploit that successfully leaks arbitrary kernel memory on a Kabi Lake CPU.  Our exploit relies on bpftool to get the eBPF's programs addresses, but this is only for simplicity. A non-privileged attacker could simply brute force collisions in the branch predictor until observing the attack succeeding.



<span class="line"><!---->Using these techniques, we built a proof-of-concept exploit that successfully leaks arbitrary kernel memory on a Kabi Lake CPU.  Our exploit relies on bpftool to get the eBPF's programs addresses, but this is only for simplicity. A non-privileged attacker could simply brute force collisions in the branch predictor until observing the attack succeeding.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





To leak the data, we use an eBPF program on another core as a "listener", with the same method used by Jann Horn here:



<span class="line"><!---->To leak the data, we use an eBPF program on another core as a "listener", with the same method used by Jann Horn here:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





    



<span class="line"><!---->    <!----></span>





https://bugs.chromium.org/p/project-zero/issues/detail?id=1711



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://bugs.chromium.org/p/project-zero/issues/detail?id=1711"><!---->https://bugs.chromium.org/p/project-zero/issues/detail?id=1711<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





We'll be happy to discuss further, including potential mitigations, as you desire.



<span class="line"><!---->We'll be happy to discuss further, including potential mitigations, as you desire.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





CREDIT INFORMATION



<b class="line"><!---->CREDIT INFORMATION<!----></b>



<br>





Reporter credit: Ofek Kirzner and Adam Morrison, Tel Aviv University, Israel



<span class="line"><!---->Reporter credit: Ofek Kirzner and Adam Morrison, Tel Aviv University, Israel<!----></span>

We've reported all 3 issues.  For eBPF, they're not convinced it's exploitable since we relied on bpftool.  We'll work on implementing the brute forcing to convince them, although it seems like jumping through hoops.



<span class="line"><!---->We've reported all 3 issues.  For eBPF, they're not convinced it's exploitable since we relied on bpftool.  We'll work on implementing the brute forcing to convince them, although it seems like jumping through hoops.<!----></span>

<br>





The other two issues they consider theoretical, therefore not sensitive, and want discussion to move to LKML.  We don't think that's a good idea at this point.



<span class="line"><!---->The other two issues they consider theoretical, therefore not sensitive, and want discussion to move to LKML.  We don't think that's a good idea at this point.<!----></span>

Thanks for the update!



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks for the update!<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Process-wise, we're intending to leave it to upstream to decide on the right approach to address the gaps, and I'm being told that conversations are already underway. Marking as Status=ExternalDependency accordingly.



<span class="line"><!---->Process-wise, we're intending to leave it to upstream to decide on the right approach to address the gaps, and I'm being told that conversations are already underway. Marking as Status=ExternalDependency accordingly.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Regarding severity rating: the worst thing to happen that I can think of is an unprivileged unsandboxed process to get an arbitrary memory read primitive for kernel memory. That could be used to exfiltrate encryption keys and other secrets (browser cookies and access tokens as well, but if you've already escalated to browser process then you already have these). A mitigating factor is that you need an initial exploit to gain code execution. Medium severity seems reasonable overall.



<span class="line"><!---->Regarding severity rating: the worst thing to happen that I can think of is an unprivileged unsandboxed process to get an arbitrary memory read primitive for kernel memory. That could be used to exfiltrate encryption keys and other secrets (browser cookies and access tokens as well, but if you've already escalated to browser process then you already have these). A mitigating factor is that you need an initial exploit to gain code execution. Medium severity seems reasonable overall.<!----></span>

       Fixes: b2157399cc98 ("bpf: prevent out-of-bounds speculation")



<span class="line"><!---->       Fixes: b2157399cc98 ("bpf: prevent out-of-bounds speculation")<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Commit b2157399cc98 was introduced after v4.14, so it is not surprising that the fix was never backported to v4.14.y and earlier. Unfortunately commit b2157399cc98  _was_ backported to v4.14.y and to v4.4.y, so the problem did find its way into those branches. Problem though is that the fixes don't apply to v4.14.y, much less to v4.4.y, and the conflicts are substantial. We don't have experience with that code, so I'd rather not touch it.



<span class="line"><!---->Commit b2157399cc98 was introduced after v4.14, so it is not surprising that the fix was never backported to v4.14.y and earlier. Problem though is that the fixes don't apply to v4.14.y, much less to v4.4.y, and the conflicts are substantial. We don't have experience with that code, so I'd rather not touch it.<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }

          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
      </style>
      <div class="chops-autocomplete-container">
        <span class="screenreader-hidden" aria-live="polite">
          
        </span>
        <table hidden="">
          <tbody>
            
          </tbody>
        </table>
      </div>
    <!----></mr-autocomplete>
            </div>
